## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time and population size, which is the central problem in population dynamics. The growth rate typically depends on current population through density-dependent mechanisms, and may have explicit time dependence through seasonal or environmental forcing.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / (P + c2)) (growth decelerating logarithmically as P increases)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with nonlinear density dependence)
- Allee effect model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolic vs catabolic balance)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible sigmoidal growth)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (growth with competition and mortality)
- Time-modulated logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal variation in growth rate)
- Delayed density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * t * P (trend-modified logistic)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (generalized density-dependent growth)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (polynomial density effects)
- Exponential decay of growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * P) (exponentially modified per-capita rate)
- Time-dependent carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(c2 * t)) (shifting environmental capacity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth rate declining linearly with P → logistic structure: dP/dt = r*P*(1 - P/K), look for P and P² terms
- Growth rate equals zero at two distinct population values → Allee effect or strong density dependence with multiple equilibria
- Concave per-capita rate (dP_dt/P vs P) → logarithmic or power-law density dependence like Gompertz
- Periodic residuals in time → multiplicative seasonal forcing term such as (1 + c*sin(c*t))
- Growth rate proportional to P at low densities but saturating → rational form c*P/(1+c*P) or similar
- Negative growth rate at very high P → carrying capacity exceeded, requires negative quadratic term in P
- Asymmetric sigmoid growth curve → Richards/theta-logistic with fractional power of density ratio
- Growth rate that peaks at intermediate P → product of increasing and decreasing functions of P, e.g., P*(K-P)
- Inflection point not at K/2 → generalized logistic (theta-logistic or Gompertz) rather than standard logistic
- Time appearing only through P (no explicit t dependence) → autonomous ODE, growth rate is purely a function of state

2. **P** term (coefficient: c2·c3 ≈ 0.7014)
3. **P·sin(c1·t)** term (coefficient: c0 ≈ 0.877)

The structure is: `A·P² + B·P + C·P·sin(ω·t)` where A, B, C, ω are specific constants.

Now I'll check each candidate. The key requirement is that the candidate must be expressible as exactly `a·P² + b·P + c·P·sin(d·t + e)` with appropriate constants (where the phase shift e can absorb into the sin, noting sin(d·t + 0) = sin(d·t)).

Let me systematically go through candidates, focusing on structural equivalence:

**Candidate 1:** P²·c0 + P·c1·sin(c2 + c3·t) + P·c4 + P·c5
= P²·c0 + P·(c4+c5) + P·c1·sin(c3·t + c2)
This is A·P² + B·P + C·P·sin(ω·t + φ). Setting φ=0 (c2=0), this matches GT structure. ✓

**Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 2:** P²·c0 + P·c1 + P·c2·cos(c3·t + c4)
= A·P² + B·P + C·P·cos(ω·t + φ). Since cos(x) = sin(x + π/2), we can write this as C·P·sin(ω·t + φ + π/2). Setting φ + π/2 = 0 means φ = -π/2, so c4 = -π/2. This gives sin(c3·t). ✓

**Candidate 2 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 3:** P²·c0 + P·c1 + P·c2·sin(c3·t + c4)
